### [1] [CamDirector: Towards Long-Term Coherent Video Trajectory Editing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02256)
*Zhihao Shi,Kejia Yin,Weilin Wan,Yuhongze Zhou,Yuanhao Yu,Xinxin Zuo,Qiang Sun,Juwei Lu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Proposes a VTE framework that explicitly aggregates video-wide information via a hybrid warping + world cache and a history-guided autoregressive diffusion, enabling precise camera control and long-term consistency; introduces the iPhone-PTZ benchmark and achieves SOTA with fewer parameters.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing video trajectory editing lacks precise camera control and long-range temporal consistency. Prior methods either encode target poses with limited-capacity embeddings or depend on single-frame warping and only implicit cross-frame aggregation in diffusion models, leading to drift and inconsistent inpainting of unseen regions.

Method: 1) Hybrid warping with explicit cross-video aggregation: static regions are accumulated into a "world cache" and rendered to target poses; dynamic regions are directly warped; their fusion produces globally consistent coarse frames that guide refinement. 2) History-guided autoregressive diffusion: processes segments conditioned on their history while incrementally updating the world cache to reinforce previously inpainted content, yielding long-term temporal coherence.

Result: State-of-the-art performance on the new iPhone-PTZ benchmark, with fewer parameters than prior methods. Qualitatively, it provides tighter camera-path adherence, globally consistent content, and more plausible inpainting across long ranges.

Conclusion: Explicit world-level aggregation combined with history-aware autoregressive diffusion improves camera controllability and temporal coherence in VTE, producing professional-looking edits while being parameter-efficient; the iPhone-PTZ benchmark supports standardized evaluation of diverse camera motions.

Abstract: Video (camera) trajectory editing aims to synthesize new videos that follow user-defined camera paths while preserving scene content and plausibly inpainting previously unseen regions, upgrading amateur footage into professionally styled videos. Existing VTE methods struggle with precise camera control and long-range consistency because they either inject target poses through a limited-capacity embedding or rely on single-frame warping with only implicit cross-frame aggregation in video diffusion models. To address these issues, we introduce a new VTE framework that 1) explicitly aggregates information across the entire source video via a hybrid warping scheme. Specifically, static regions are progressively fused into a world cache then rendered to target camera poses, while dynamic regions are directly warped; their fusion yields globally consistent coarse frames that guide refinement. 2) processes video segments jointly with their history via a history-guided autoregressive diffusion model, while the world cache is incrementally updated to reinforce already inpainted content, enabling long-term temporal coherence. Finally, we present iPhone-PTZ, a new VTE benchmark with diverse camera motions and large trajectory variations, and achieve state-of-the-art performance with fewer parameters.

</details>


### [2] [Social-JEPA: Emergent Geometric Isomorphism](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02263)
*Haoran Zhang,Youjin Wang,Yi Duan,Rong Fu,Dianyu Zhao,Sicheng Fan,Shuaishuai Cao,Wentao Guo,Xiao Zhou*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Separately trained predictive world models from different camera views end up with latent spaces that are linearly, near-isometrically aligned, enabling zero-shot transfer of classifiers and faster, cheaper subsequent learning via representation translation/distillation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understand whether self-supervised predictive objectives impose geometric regularities on learned representations across independently trained agents, and whether such regularities can enable interoperability in decentralized vision systems without coordination or shared data/parameters.

Method: Train independent agents to learn world models (predictive latent representations) from distinct viewpoints with no parameter sharing. After training, analyze the geometry of their latent spaces and fit simple linear mappings to relate them. Evaluate robustness to viewpoint shifts and low pixel overlap, test zero-shot porting of classifiers via latent translation, and assess compute savings from distillation-like migration.

Result: The agents’ latent spaces are related by an approximate linear isometry despite disparate views, allowing transparent translation between representations. A classifier trained on one agent transfers to the other with no additional gradient steps. Using the alignment for distillation-like migration speeds up later learning and substantially reduces total compute. The geometric alignment persists under large viewpoint differences and minimal pixel overlap.

Conclusion: Predictive learning strongly constrains representation geometry, leading to emergent cross-agent linear isometries. This provides a lightweight path to interoperability—zero-shot model porting and efficient knowledge transfer—among decentralized vision systems.

Abstract: World models compress rich sensory streams into compact latent codes that anticipate future observations. We let separate agents acquire such models from distinct viewpoints of the same environment without any parameter sharing or coordination. After training, their internal representations exhibit a striking emergent property: the two latent spaces are related by an approximate linear isometry, enabling transparent translation between them. This geometric consensus survives large viewpoint shifts and scant overlap in raw pixels. Leveraging the learned alignment, a classifier trained on one agent can be ported to the other with no additional gradient steps, while distillation-like migration accelerates later learning and markedly reduces total compute. The findings reveal that predictive learning objectives impose strong regularities on representation geometry, suggesting a lightweight path to interoperability among decentralized vision systems. The code is available at https://anonymous.4open.science/r/Social-JEPA-5C57.

</details>


### [3] [From Visual to Multimodal: Systematic Ablation of Encoders and Fusion Strategies in Animal Identification](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02270)
*Vasiliy Kudryavtsev,Kirill Borodin,German Berezin,Kirill Bubenchikov,Grach Mkrtchian,Alexander Ryzhkov*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They propose a multimodal pet verification system that enriches visual embeddings with synthetic text-based identity priors and fuse them via a gated mechanism, trained on a 1.9M-photo, ~695k-animal corpus, achieving 84.28% Top-1 and 0.0422 EER—about 11% better than unimodal baselines.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Pet re-identification systems are hindered by small datasets and reliance on a single (visual) modality, which limits robustness and accuracy in real-world lost-pet matching. Adding complementary semantic cues could improve discrimination, especially at large scale.

Method: Build a large-scale corpus (1.9M photos, 695,091 animals). Generate synthetic textual descriptions to serve as semantic identity priors. Conduct ablations to choose backbones (SigLIP2-Giant for vision, E5-Small-v2 for text). Evaluate multimodal fusion strategies and adopt a gated fusion mechanism for verification.

Result: The gated fusion model achieved 84.28% Top-1 accuracy and 0.0422 EER on a comprehensive test protocol, delivering an ~11% absolute improvement over strong unimodal baselines.

Conclusion: Integrating synthesized semantic descriptions with visual features via adaptive gating sharpens decision boundaries and substantially boosts large-scale pet re-identification performance, demonstrating clear advantages over unimodal approaches.

Abstract: Automated animal identification is a practical task for reuniting lost pets with their owners, yet current systems often struggle due to limited dataset scale and reliance on unimodal visual cues. This study introduces a multimodal verification framework that enhances visual features with semantic identity priors derived from synthetic textual descriptions. We constructed a massive training corpus of 1.9 million photographs covering 695,091~unique animals to support this investigation. Through systematic ablation studies, we identified SigLIP2-Giant and E5-Small-v2 as the optimal vision and text backbones. We further evaluated fusion strategies ranging from simple concatenation to adaptive gating to determine the best method for integrating these modalities. Our proposed approach utilizes a gated fusion mechanism and achieved a Top-1 accuracy of 84.28\% and an Equal Error Rate of 0.0422 on a comprehensive test protocol. These results represent an 11\% improvement over leading unimodal baselines and demonstrate that integrating synthesized semantic descriptions significantly refines decision boundaries in large-scale pet re-identification.

</details>


### [4] [Beyond Prompt Degradation: Prototype-guided Dual-pool Prompting for Incremental Object Detection](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02286)
*Yaoteng Zhang,Zhou Qing,Junyu Gao,Qi Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: PDP is a prompt-decoupled incremental object detection framework that uses dual prompt pools (shared/general and private/task-specific) plus a prototypical pseudo-labeling module to prevent prompt coupling/drift, achieving state-of-the-art gains on COCO and VOC.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Prompt-based, replay-free IOD is parameter-efficient but degrades over time due to prompt coupling and drift caused by inconsistent supervision (old classes mislabeled as background). A method is needed to preserve past knowledge while adapting to new classes without replay.

Method: A dual-pool prompt design: a shared pool captures task-general knowledge for forward transfer, and a private pool learns task-specific discriminative features, explicitly decoupling prompts to avoid interference. A Prototypical Pseudo-Label Generation (PPG) module dynamically updates class prototype space during training and filters pseudo-labels using prototypes to keep supervision consistent across increments.

Result: State-of-the-art performance with +9.2% AP on MS-COCO and +3.3% AP on PASCAL VOC over prior methods; code and data released.

Conclusion: Decoupling task-general and task-specific prompts and enforcing prototype-guided pseudo-label consistency mitigates prompt degradation, better balancing stability and plasticity for incremental object detection.

Abstract: Incremental Object Detection (IOD) aims to continuously learn new object categories without forgetting previously learned ones. Recently, prompt-based methods have gained popularity for their replay-free design and parameter efficiency. However, due to prompt coupling and prompt drift, these methods often suffer from prompt degradation during continual adaptation. To address these issues, we propose a novel prompt-decoupled framework called PDP. PDP innovatively designs a dual-pool prompt decoupling paradigm, which consists of a shared pool used to capture task-general knowledge for forward transfer, and a private pool used to learn task-specific discriminative features. This paradigm explicitly separates task-general and task-specific prompts, preventing interference between prompts and mitigating prompt coupling. In addition, to counteract prompt drift resulting from inconsistent supervision where old foreground objects are treated as background in subsequent tasks, PDP introduces a Prototypical Pseudo-Label Generation (PPG) module. PPG can dynamically update the class prototype space during training and use the class prototypes to further filter valuable pseudo-labels, maintaining supervisory signal consistency throughout the incremental process. PDP achieves state-of-the-art performance on MS-COCO (with a 9.2\% AP improvement) and PASCAL VOC (with a 3.3\% AP improvement) benchmarks, highlighting its potential in balancing stability and plasticity. The code and dataset are released at: https://github.com/zyt95579/PDP\_IOD/tree/main

</details>


### [5] [AutoFFS: Adversarial Deformations for Facial Feminization Surgery Planning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02288)
*Paul Friedrich,Florentin Bieder,Florian M. Thieringer,Philippe C. Cattin*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: AutoFFS generates counterfactual, feminized skull morphologies by adversarially deforming patient skull shapes using sex-classifier feedback, offering quantitative guidance for facial feminization surgery planning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: FFS planning is largely subjective and lacks quantitative, reproducible anatomical targets. The authors aim to provide data-driven, patient-specific guidance grounded in learned sexual dimorphism.

Method: Train an ensemble of binary sex classifiers on skull shapes; then perform deformation-based targeted adversarial attacks via free-form deformations to morph an individual skull toward the target sex while preserving anatomical plausibility. The ensemble guides the deformation to encode sexual dimorphism. Outputs are counterfactual skull morphologies for planning.

Result: Generated morphologies are judged as the target sex by the classifier ensemble and by a human perceptual study, indicating that the deformations capture salient sex-related craniofacial traits.

Conclusion: AutoFFS offers a quantitative, reproducible framework for preoperative planning in FFS by proposing patient-specific target skull shapes. Early validation shows perceptual alignment, suggesting clinical promise, though broader clinical evaluation and safety/feasibility studies are needed.

Abstract: Facial feminization surgery (FFS) is a key component of gender affirmation for transgender and gender diverse patients, aiming to reshape craniofacial structures toward a female morphology. Current surgical planning procedures largely rely on subjective clinical assessment, lacking quantitative and reproducible anatomical guidance. We therefore propose AutoFFS, a novel data-driven framework that generates counterfactual skull morphologies through adversarial free-form deformations. Our method performs a deformation-based targeted adversarial attack on an ensemble of pre-trained binary sex classifiers that learned sexual dimorphism, effectively transforming individual skull shapes toward the target sex. The generated counterfactual skull morphologies provide a quantitative foundation for preoperative planning in FFS, driving advances in this largely overlooked patient group. We validate our approach through classifier-based evaluation and a human perceptual study, confirming that the generated morphologies exhibit target sex characteristics.

</details>


### [6] [HAMMER: Harnessing MLLM via Cross-Modal Integration for Intention-Driven 3D Affordance Grounding](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02329)
*Lei Yao,Yong Chen,Yuejiao Su,Yi Wang,Moyun Liu,Lap-Pui Chau*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: HAMMER is an MLLM-guided, intention-driven framework for 3D affordance grounding that converts observed human–object interactions into a contact-aware embedding, fuses cross-modal cues hierarchically, lifts them into geometry-aware features, and achieves state-of-the-art, robust localization across standard and corrupted benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Humans infer object affordances from observing interactions and generalize to new objects. Existing 3D affordance methods often depend on explicit attribute descriptions or 2D segmenters, which can miss contextual semantics and be brittle. The goal is to exploit multimodal LLMs to capture interaction intention and context for more generalizable, robust 3D affordance grounding.

Method: 1) Extract a contact-aware, interaction-intention embedding from images; 2) use it to infer textual affordance labels via an MLLM, encouraging rich semantic/context capture; 3) apply a hierarchical cross-modal integration mechanism to refine 3D representations with complementary MLLM information; 4) use a multi-granular geometry lifting module to inject spatial characteristics into the intention embedding, enabling precise 3D localization; 5) evaluate on public datasets and a newly constructed corrupted benchmark.

Result: Across multiple public datasets and a new corruption benchmark, HAMMER outperforms prior methods in 3D affordance localization and shows stronger robustness under input degradations. (Exact metrics not provided in the abstract.)

Conclusion: Intention-driven, cross-modal integration combined with geometry-aware lifting enables accurate and robust 3D affordance grounding that generalizes to novel objects. Results indicate superiority over existing approaches; resources (code and weights) are available for reproducibility.

Abstract: Humans commonly identify 3D object affordance through observed interactions in images or videos, and once formed, such knowledge can be generically generalized to novel objects. Inspired by this principle, we advocate for a novel framework that leverages emerging multimodal large language models (MLLMs) for interaction intention-driven 3D affordance grounding, namely HAMMER. Instead of generating explicit object attribute descriptions or relying on off-the-shelf 2D segmenters, we alternatively aggregate the interaction intention depicted in the image into a contact-aware embedding and guide the model to infer textual affordance labels, ensuring it thoroughly excavates object semantics and contextual cues. We further devise a hierarchical cross-modal integration mechanism to fully exploit the complementary information from the MLLM for 3D representation refinement and introduce a multi-granular geometry lifting module that infuses spatial characteristics into the extracted intention embedding, thus facilitating accurate 3D affordance localization. Extensive experiments on public datasets and our newly constructed corrupted benchmark demonstrate the superiority and robustness of HAMMER compared to existing approaches. All code and weights are publicly available.

</details>


### [7] [MERG3R: A Divide-and-Conquer Approach to Large-Scale Neural Visual Geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02351)
*Leo Kaixuan Cheng,Abdus Shaikh,Ruofan Liang,Zhijie Wu,Yushi Guan,Nandita Vijaykumar*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: MERG3R is a training-free, model-agnostic divide-and-conquer framework that lets memory-hungry neural geometry models (e.g., VGGT, Pi3) scale to large, unordered image sets by partitioning them into overlapping subsets, reconstructing locally, and merging via global alignment and confidence-weighted bundle adjustment, yielding more accurate, memory-efficient, and scalable 3D reconstructions on multiple benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Transformer-based neural visual geometry models rely on full attention and thus hit GPU memory limits, preventing their use on large, unordered image collections. There is a need to scale such models without retraining while preserving or improving reconstruction quality.

Method: 1) Reorder and partition unordered images into overlapping, geometrically diverse subsets. 2) Independently reconstruct each subset using existing neural geometry models. 3) Merge local reconstructions with efficient global alignment and confidence-weighted bundle adjustment to enforce global consistency. The pipeline is training-free and model-agnostic.

Result: Across 7-Scenes, NRGBD, Tanks & Temples, and Cambridge Landmarks, the framework consistently improves reconstruction accuracy, memory efficiency, and scalability, enabling high-quality reconstructions even when the dataset exceeds native memory limits.

Conclusion: Divide-and-conquer plus confidence-weighted global merging overcomes the memory bottleneck of full-attention neural geometry models, extending them to large-scale, unordered image collections without retraining and producing globally consistent 3D models.

Abstract: Recent advancements in neural visual geometry, including transformer-based models such as VGGT and Pi3, have achieved impressive accuracy on 3D reconstruction tasks. However, their reliance on full attention makes them fundamentally limited by GPU memory capacity, preventing them from scaling to large, unordered image collections. We introduce MERG3R, a training-free divide-and-conquer framework that enables geometric foundation models to operate far beyond their native memory limits. MERG3R first reorders and partitions unordered images into overlapping, geometrically diverse subsets that can be reconstructed independently. It then merges the resulting local reconstructions through an efficient global alignment and confidence-weighted bundle adjustment procedure, producing a globally consistent 3D model. Our framework is model-agnostic and can be paired with existing neural geometry models. Across large-scale datasets, including 7-Scenes, NRGBD, Tanks & Temples, and Cambridge Landmarks, MERG3R consistently improves reconstruction accuracy, memory efficiency, and scalability, enabling high-quality reconstruction when the dataset exceeds memory capacity limits.

</details>


### [8] [Beyond Caption-Based Queries for Video Moment Retrieval](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02363)
*David Pujol-Perich,Albert Clapés,Dima Damen,Sergio Escalera,Michael Wray*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They show that DETR-based video moment retrieval models trained on caption-style queries fail to generalize to real search queries due to a language gap and a multi-moment gap, diagnose a decoder query collapse as a root cause, and fix it with architectural tweaks that increase active decoder queries, yielding large mAP gains on new search-style benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Real-world users issue short, under-specified search queries, but most VMR models are trained and evaluated on rich caption-style queries. This train–test mismatch degrades performance, especially when queries refer to multiple temporal moments. The work aims to quantify this gap, understand why DETR-style VMR fails, and make models robust to search queries.

Method: 1) Construct three search-style VMR benchmarks by rewriting queries in HD-EPIC, YouCook2, and ActivityNet-Captions. 2) Analyze generalization failures, identifying (i) a language gap from under-specified search language and (ii) a multi-moment gap from single- to multi-moment queries. 3) Diagnose an active decoder-query collapse in DETR architectures that limits coverage of multiple moments. 4) Propose architectural modifications that increase the number of active decoder queries to better cover diverse temporal regions.

Result: On search-style queries, their method improves up to +14.82% mAP_m overall and up to +21.83% mAP_m on multi-moment queries across the three datasets, with extensive experiments validating the approach.

Conclusion: Bridging the caption-to-search mismatch in VMR requires both evaluation that reflects real search behavior and architectures that avoid decoder-query collapse. Increasing active decoder queries substantially improves generalization to under-specified and multi-moment search queries; released code, models, and data enable further research.

Abstract: In this work, we investigate the degradation of existing VMR methods, particularly of DETR architectures, when trained on caption-based queries but evaluated on search queries. For this, we introduce three benchmarks by modifying the textual queries in three public VMR datasets -- i.e., HD-EPIC, YouCook2 and ActivityNet-Captions. Our analysis reveals two key generalization challenges: (i) A language gap, arising from the linguistic under-specification of search queries, and (ii) a multi-moment gap, caused by the shift from single-moment to multi-moment queries. We also identify a critical issue in these architectures -- an active decoder-query collapse -- as a primary cause of the poor generalization to multi-moment instances. We mitigate this issue with architectural modifications that effectively increase the number of active decoder queries. Extensive experiments demonstrate that our approach improves performance on search queries by up to 14.82% mAP_m, and up to 21.83% mAP_m on multi-moment search queries. The code, models and data are available in the project webpage: https://davidpujol.github.io/beyond-vmr/

</details>


### [9] [Retrieving Patient-Specific Radiomic Feature Sets for Transparent Knee MRI Assessment](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02367)
*Yaxi Chen,Simin Ni,Jingjing Zhang,Shaheer U. Saeed,Yipei Wang,Aleksandra Ivanova,Rikin Hargunani,Chaozong Liu,Jie Huang,Yipeng Hu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They replace per-feature top‑k selection in radiomics with a patient‑specific selection of a compact, diverse feature set using a two‑stage retrieval (candidate sampling + learned set scorer), yielding better accuracy than top‑k while keeping interpretability competitive with deep nets.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Radiomics offers transparency versus end‑to‑end deep learning but often underperforms because it relies on static, population‑level feature pools and marginal top‑k weighting that admits redundant features and misses complementary interactions. The authors aim to improve performance without sacrificing interpretability by tailoring feature sets to each patient.

Method: Formulate feature selection as choosing a single compact set per subject. Use a two‑stage retrieval to avoid combinatorial search: (1) randomly sample diverse candidate feature sets from a large radiomic pool; (2) score and rank these sets with a learned feature‑set scorer, then use the best‑scoring set with a classifier for diagnosis. Demonstrate that this approximates exhaustive k‑feature selection.

Result: On ACL tear detection and Kellgren–Lawrence osteoarthritis grading, their approach outperforms classical adaptive radiomics that keep top‑k features by marginal weights (for the same k) and is competitive with end‑to‑end deep learning, while preserving transparency. Generated sets map to anatomical regions and radiomic families for auditability.

Conclusion: Patient‑specific, diversity‑aware feature‑set selection via two‑stage retrieval can close the accuracy gap to deep models while maintaining interpretability. The method yields compact, auditable feature sets that better capture complementary evidence than marginal top‑k schemes.

Abstract: Classical radiomic features are designed to quantify image appearance and intensity patterns. Compared with end-to-end deep learning (DL) models trained for disease classification, radiomics pipelines with low-dimensional parametric classifiers offer enhanced transparency and interpretability, yet often underperform because of the reliance on population-level predefined feature sets. Recent work on adaptive radiomics uses DL to predict feature weights over a radiomic pool, then thresholds these weights to retain the top-k features from large radiomic pool F (often ~10^3). However, such marginal ranking can over-admit redundant descriptors and overlook complementary feature interactions. We propose a patient-specific feature-set selection framework that predicts a single compact feature set per subject, targeting complementary and diverse evidence rather than marginal top-k features. To overcome the intractable combinatorial search space of F choose k features, our method utilizes a 2-stage retrieval strategy: randomly sample diverse candidate feature sets, then rank these sets with a learned scoring function to select a high-performing feature set for the specific patient. The system consists of a feature-set scorer, and a classifier that performs the final diagnosis. We empirically show that the proposed two-stage retrieval approximates the original exhaustive all k-feature selection. Validating on tasks including ACL tear detection and KL grading for osteoarthritis, the experimental results achieve diagnostic performance, outperforming the top-k approach with the same k values, and competitive with end-to-end DL models while maintaining high transparency. The model generates auditable feature sets that link clinical outcomes to specific anatomical regions and radiomic families, allowing clinicians to inspect which anatomical structures and quantitative descriptors drive the prediction.

</details>


### [10] [Cultural Counterfactuals: Evaluating Cultural Biases in Large Vision-Language Models with Counterfactual Examples](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02370)
*Phillip Howard,Xin Su,Kathleen C. Fraser*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Introduces Cultural Counterfactuals, a ~60k-image synthetic dataset that edits the same people into diverse cultural contexts (religion, nationality, socioeconomic status) to precisely measure cultural biases in LVLMs, demonstrating its utility on popular models.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Bias work on LVLMs has largely centered on visible demographics (e.g., race, gender), leaving culturally grounded biases (religion, nationality, SES) underexplored because cultural group membership depends on contextual cues that current datasets lack. A controlled resource is needed to isolate the effect of cultural context on model outputs.

Method: Construct a high-quality synthetic, counterfactual image dataset by using an image-editing model to place people of varying demographics into real cultural context scenes. For each person, create multiple counterfactual contexts across religion, nationality, and SES, enabling within-person comparisons to isolate context effects. Use these counterfactual sets to probe LVLMs and compare outputs across contexts.

Result: Generated nearly 60k counterfactual images and showed that comparing LVLM outputs across matched counterfactuals enables quantification of cultural biases in popular LVLMs. (The abstract does not report specific metrics, only that biases can be quantified using the dataset.)

Conclusion: Cultural Counterfactuals offers a practical, controlled way to measure how cultural context shapes LVLM behavior, filling a key data gap beyond visibly identifiable demographics and supporting more comprehensive bias evaluation and potential mitigation.

Abstract: Large Vision-Language Models (LVLMs) have grown increasingly powerful in recent years, but can also exhibit harmful biases. Prior studies investigating such biases have primarily focused on demographic traits related to the visual characteristics of a person depicted in an image, such as their race or gender. This has left biases related to cultural differences (e.g., religion, socioeconomic status), which cannot be readily discerned from an individual's appearance alone, relatively understudied. A key challenge in measuring cultural biases is that determining which group an individual belongs to often depends upon cultural context cues in images, and datasets annotated with cultural context cues are lacking. To address this gap, we introduce Cultural Counterfactuals: a high-quality synthetic dataset containing nearly 60k counterfactual images for measuring cultural biases related to religion, nationality, and socioeconomic status. To ensure that cultural contexts are accurately depicted, we generate our dataset using an image-editing model to place people of different demographics into real cultural context images. This enables the construction of counterfactual image sets which depict the same person in multiple different contexts, allowing for precise measurement of the impact that cultural context differences have on LVLM outputs. We demonstrate the utility of Cultural Counterfactuals for quantifying cultural biases in popular LVLMs.

</details>


### [11] [Aligning Fetal Anatomy with Kinematic Tree Log-Euclidean PolyRigid Transforms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02371)
*Yingcheng Liu,Athena Taymourtash,Yang Liu,Esra Abaci Turk,William M. Wells,Leo Joskowicz,P. Ellen Grant,Polina Golland*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: They propose a differentiable, volumetric SMPL-style model driven by a new KTPolyRigid transform to achieve smooth, bijective deformations for articulated anatomy, reducing foldings and improving registration and label-efficient segmentation on fetal MRI.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Surface-based body models used in medical imaging ignore internal volumetric structure and common deformation schemes can violate anatomical consistency (e.g., introduce foldings). A volumetric, anatomically consistent mapping is needed for articulated bodies such as fetuses in MRI.

Method: Develop a Kinematic Tree-based Log-Euclidean PolyRigid (KTPolyRigid) transform integrated into a differentiable volumetric extension of SMPL. The kinematic-tree parameterization and log-Euclidean composition resolve Lie algebra ambiguities in large, non-local articulated motions and encourage smooth, bijective volumetric mappings. The framework supports groupwise registration and template-based segmentation.

Result: On 53 fetal MRI volumes, KTPolyRigid yields deformation fields with significantly fewer folding artifacts than baselines, enabling robust groupwise image registration and label-efficient, template-based segmentation of fetal organs.

Conclusion: KTPolyRigid-based volumetric modeling offers anatomically consistent deformations and a practical foundation for standardized volumetric analysis of articulated bodies, demonstrated on fetal MRI with improved deformation quality and downstream tasks.

Abstract: Automated analysis of articulated bodies is crucial in medical imaging. Existing surface-based models often ignore internal volumetric structures and rely on deformation methods that lack anatomical consistency guarantees. To address this problem, we introduce a differentiable volumetric body model based on the Skinned Multi-Person Linear (SMPL) formulation, driven by a new Kinematic Tree-based Log-Euclidean PolyRigid (KTPolyRigid) transform. KTPolyRigid resolves Lie algebra ambiguities associated with large, non-local articulated motions, and encourages smooth, bijective volumetric mappings. Evaluated on 53 fetal MRI volumes, KTPolyRigid yields deformation fields with significantly fewer folding artifacts. Furthermore, our framework enables robust groupwise image registration and a label-efficient, template-based segmentation of fetal organs. It provides a robust foundation for standardized volumetric analysis of articulated bodies in medical imaging.

</details>


### [12] [Advancing Earth Observation Through Machine Learning: A TorchGeo Tutorial](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02386)
*Caleb Robinson,Nils Lehmann,Adam J. Stewart,Burak Ekim,Heng Fang,Isaac A. Corley,Mauricio Cordeiro*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Presents a hands-on tutorial for TorchGeo, a PyTorch geospatial library, demonstrating core abstractions and an end-to-end Sentinel‑2 water-segmentation workflow that outputs GeoTIFF predictions, with reproducible notebooks provided.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Earth observation ML differs from standard vision—data are large georeferenced scenes, labels can be rasters or vectors in varied CRS, and spatially aware sampling/splitting is required. There is a need for tools that simplify these geospatial-specific challenges and standardize workflows.

Method: Introduce TorchGeo’s datasets, samplers, transforms, and pretrained models via code examples, then conduct a case study training a semantic segmentation model for multispectral water detection using Sentinel‑2 imagery and the Earth Surface Water dataset; apply the model to a Rio de Janeiro scene and export predictions as a GeoTIFF.

Result: Demonstrates that TorchGeo supports an end-to-end geospatial ML pipeline: training a water-segmentation model, running inference on a real Sentinel‑2 scene, and producing georeferenced outputs. The full workflow is packaged into two publicly available notebooks.

Conclusion: TorchGeo lowers the barrier for spatially aware ML on Earth observation data and provides practical, reproducible guidance for building end-to-end geospatial segmentation workflows, facilitating broader and more reliable adoption in the community.

Abstract: Earth observation machine learning pipelines differ fundamentally from standard computer vision workflows. Imagery is typically delivered as large, georeferenced scenes, labels may be raster masks or vector geometries in distinct coordinate reference systems, and both training and evaluation often require spatially aware sampling and splitting strategies. TorchGeo is a PyTorch-based domain library that provides datasets, samplers, transforms and pre-trained models with the goal of making it easy to use geospatial data in machine learning pipelines. In this paper, we introduce a tutorial that demonstrates 1.) the core TorchGeo abstractions through code examples, and 2.) an end-to-end case study on multispectral water segmentation from Sentinel-2 imagery using the Earth Surface Water dataset. This demonstrates how to train a semantic segmentation model using TorchGeo datasets, apply the model to a Sentinel-2 scene over Rio de Janeiro, Brazil, and save the resulting predictions as a GeoTIFF for further geospatial analysis. The tutorial code itself is distributed as two Python notebooks: https://torchgeo.readthedocs.io/en/stable/tutorials/torchgeo.html and https://torchgeo.readthedocs.io/en/stable/tutorials/earth_surface_water.html.

*My H. Dinh,Aditya Sant,Akshay Malhotra,Keya Patani,Shahab Hamidi-Rad*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: QuADD is a quantization‑aware dataset distillation framework that co-optimizes the number of synthetic samples and their precision under a fixed bit budget, yielding higher accuracy per bit than prior DD and post-quantized baselines on images and 3GPP beam management.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing dataset distillation largely focuses on reducing sample count while overlooking how data precision (bitwidth) affects storage/training efficiency and performance. There is a need to explicitly manage the trade-off between how many samples are stored and how precisely they are represented under a fixed memory/bit budget, grounded in a rate–distortion perspective.

Method: Integrate a differentiable quantization module into the distillation loop to enable end-to-end co-optimization of synthetic examples and quantization parameters. Enforce a fixed bit budget and allocate bits between sample count and per-sample precision. Support both uniform and adaptive non-uniform quantization, with the latter learning levels from data to better capture information-dense regions.

Result: Empirically study how bit allocation impacts learning and show that QuADD achieves superior accuracy per bit compared to existing DD and post-quantization baselines across image classification and 3GPP beam management tasks.

Conclusion: Jointly optimizing dataset compactness and precision via quantization-aware distillation improves information efficiency. Learning adaptive non-uniform quantization further boosts performance, establishing a stronger standard for accuracy per bit across tasks.

Abstract: Dataset Distillation (DD) compresses large datasets into compact synthetic ones that maintain training performance. However, current methods mainly target sample reduction, with limited consideration of data precision and its impact on efficiency. We propose Quantization-aware Dataset Distillation (QuADD), a unified framework that jointly optimizes dataset compactness and precision under fixed bit budgets. QuADD integrates a differentiable quantization module within the distillation loop, enabling end-to-end co-optimization of synthetic samples and quantization parameters. Guided by the rate-distortion perspective, we empirically analyze how bit allocation between sample count and precision influences learning performance. Our framework supports both uniform and adaptive non-uniform quantization, where the latter learns quantization levels from data to represent information-dense regions better. Experiments on image classification and 3GPP beam management tasks show that QuADD surpasses existing DD and post-quantized baselines in accuracy per bit, establishing a new standard for information-efficient dataset distillation.

To address this, we introduce MIRAGE, a novel framework that reframes the missing-MRI problem as an anatomy-guided cross-modal latent distillation task. First, MIRAGE leverages a Biomedical Knowledge Graph (KG) and Graph Attention Networks to map heterogeneous EHR variables into a unified embedding space that can be propagated from cohorts with real MRIs to cohorts without them. To bridge the semantic gap and enforce physical spatial awareness, we employ a frozen pre-trained 3D U-Net decoder strictly as an auxiliary regularization engine. Supported by a novel cohort-aggregated skip feature compensation strategy, this decoder acts as a rigorous structural penalty, forcing 1D latent representations to encode biologically plausible, macro-level pathological semantics. By exclusively utilizing this distilled "diagnostic-surrogate" representation during inference, MIRAGE completely bypasses computationally expensive 3D voxel reconstruction. Experiments demonstrate that our framework successfully bridges the missing-modality gap, improving the AD classification rate by 13% compared to unimodal baselines in cohorts without real MRIs.

Our framework leverages a set of specialized AI agents, each dedicated to a distinct modality, enabling fine-grained understanding and collaborative reasoning across diverse document components. To ensure answer reliability, ORCA employs a debate mechanism with stress-testing, and when necessary, a thesis-antithesis adjudication process. Method: E2E-GNet introduces: (1) a geometric transformation layer to jointly optimize skeleton motion sequences on the non-Euclidean space; (2) a differentiable logarithm map activation to project them into a linear (Euclidean) space; and (3) a distortion-aware optimization layer that limits projection-induced skeleton shape distortions. The model is trained end-to-end and assessed with ablations to quantify each component’s effect.

Result: On five datasets spanning three domains, E2E-GNet surpasses competing methods with lower computational cost, and ablation studies show each proposed layer contributes to performance gains.

To this end, we propose E2E-GNet, an end-to-end geometric deep neural network for skeleton-based human motion recognition. To enhance the discriminative power between different motions in the non-Euclidean space, E2E-GNet introduces a geometric transformation layer that jointly optimizes skeleton motion sequences on this space and applies a differentiable logarithm map activation to project them onto a linear space. Building on this, we further design a distortion-aware optimization layer that limits skeleton shape distortions caused by this projection, enabling the network to retain discriminative geometric cues and achieve a higher motion recognition rate. We demonstrate the impact of each layer through ablation studies and extensive experiments across five datasets spanning three domains show that E2E-GNet outperforms other methods with lower cost.

  In this work, we introduce WTHaar-Net, a convolutional neural network that replaces the Hadamard Transform used in prior hybrid architectures with the Haar Wavelet Transform (HWT). Unlike the Hadamard Transform, the Haar transform provides spatially localized, multi-resolution representations that align more closely with the inductive biases of vision tasks. We show that the HWT admits a quantum realization using structured Hadamard gates, enabling its decomposition into unitary operations suitable for quantum circuits.
  Experiments on CIFAR-10 and Tiny-ImageNet demonstrate that WTHaar-Net achieves substantial parameter reduction while maintaining competitive accuracy. On Tiny-ImageNet, our approach outperforms both ResNet and Hadamard-based baselines. ### [24] [SGMA: Semantic-Guided Modality-Aware Segmentation for Remote Sensing with Incomplete Multimodal Data](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02505)
*Lekang Wen,Liang Liao,Jing Xiao,Mi Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Proposes SGMA, a semantics-guided, modality-aware framework that balances multimodal learning for incomplete multimodal semantic segmentation, reducing intra-class variation and cross-modal inconsistencies, and achieving SOTA gains—especially on fragile modalities.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Incomplete multimodal semantic segmentation (IMSS) suffers from (1) modality imbalance where strong modalities dominate, (2) large intra-class variation across modalities (scale/shape/orientation), and (3) cross-modal heterogeneity with conflicting cues. Prior contrastive/joint-optimization methods can over-align (losing modality-specific cues) and train imbalancedly, while overlooking intra-class variation and heterogeneity.

Method: SGMA adds two plug-and-play modules: (1) Semantic-Guided Fusion (SGF) learns multi-scale, class-wise semantic prototypes shared across modalities, estimates per-modality robustness via prototype–feature alignment, and performs adaptive, robustness-weighted fusion to mitigate intra-class variation and cross-modal inconsistencies; (2) Modality-Aware Sampling (MAS) uses the robustness scores to dynamically reweight training, emphasizing hard samples and fragile modalities to correct modality imbalance.

Result: Across multiple datasets and backbones, SGMA consistently outperforms state-of-the-art methods, with notably larger improvements on fragile (weaker) modalities. (No specific numbers given in the abstract.)

Conclusion: Semantic guidance coupled with modality-aware robustness estimation enables balanced fusion and sampling that reduces intra-class variation and reconciles cross-modal heterogeneity, improving IMSS performance and generalizing across architectures via plug-and-play modules.

Abstract: Multimodal semantic segmentation integrates complementary information from diverse sensors for remote sensing Earth observation. However, practical systems often encounter missing modalities due to sensor failures or incomplete coverage, termed Incomplete Multimodal Semantic Segmentation (IMSS). IMSS faces three key challenges: (1) multimodal imbalance, where dominant modalities suppress fragile ones; (2) intra-class variation in scale, shape, and orientation across modalities; and (3) cross-modal heterogeneity with conflicting cues producing inconsistent semantic responses. Existing methods rely on contrastive learning or joint optimization, which risk over-alignment, discarding modality-specific cues or imbalanced training, favoring robust modalities, while largely overlooking intra-class variation and cross-modal heterogeneity. To address these limitations, we propose the Semantic-Guided Modality-Aware (SGMA) framework, which ensures balanced multimodal learning while reducing intra-class variation and reconciling cross-modal inconsistencies through semantic guidance. SGMA introduces two complementary plug-and-play modules: (1) Semantic-Guided Fusion (SGF) module extracts multi-scale, class-wise semantic prototypes that capture consistent categorical representations across modalities, estimates per-modality robustness based on prototype-feature alignment, and performs adaptive fusion weighted by robustness scores to mitigate intra-class variation and cross-modal heterogeneity; (2) Modality-Aware Sampling (MAS) module leverages robustness estimations from SGF to dynamically reweight training samples, prioritizing challenging samples from fragile modalities to address modality imbalance. Extensive experiments across multiple datasets and backbones demonstrate that SGMA consistently outperforms state-of-the-art methods, with particularly significant improvements in fragile modalities.

### [27] [EIMC: Efficient Instance-aware Multi-modal Collaborative Perception](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02532)
*Kang Yang,Peng Wang,Lantao Li,Tianci Bu,Chen Sun,Deying Li,Yongcai Wang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: EIMC introduces early, instance-centric collaboration for multi-modal autonomous driving perception, injecting lightweight neighbor voxels into local fusion and selectively exchanging Top-K instance features guided by confidence heatmaps—achieving strong accuracy with ~88% less bandwidth.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current multi-modal collaborative methods first fuse modalities locally, then transmit large feature maps for collaboration, which is bandwidth-heavy and can suffer from cross-modal misalignment and missed occluded objects. There is a need to communicate only what matters, earlier, to improve safety and scalability.

Method: 1) Early collaborative voxels: neighbors send lightweight collaborative voxels that are injected into the ego agent’s local modality fusion to create compact 3D collaborative priors and tighten cross-modal alignment. 2) Heatmap-driven consensus: compute per-pixel confidence heatmaps; identify low-confidence/high-discrepancy regions; query only Top-K instance vectors from peers and fuse them with cross-attention to complete missing info. 3) Refinement fusion: gather Top-K most confident instances from each agent and enhance them via self-attention. Instance-centric messaging minimizes redundancy while preserving critical cues, especially for occlusions.

Result: On OPV2V and DAIR-V2X, EIMC attains 73.01% AP@0.5 and reduces byte-level bandwidth by 87.98% compared to the best published multi-modal collaborative detector; it recovers critical occluded objects while cutting communication load.

Conclusion: Early collaboration plus selective, instance-focused communication aligns modalities better and targets information exchange to where it’s needed, delivering high detection accuracy with drastically lower bandwidth—promising for safer, scalable V2X perception systems.

Abstract: Multi-modal collaborative perception calls for great attention to enhancing the safety of autonomous driving. However, current multi-modal approaches remain a ``local fusion to communication'' sequence, which fuses multi-modal data locally and needs high bandwidth to transmit an individual's feature data before collaborative fusion. EIMC innovatively proposes an early collaborative paradigm. It injects lightweight collaborative voxels, transmitted by neighbor agents, into the ego's local modality-fusion step, yielding compact yet informative 3D collaborative priors that tighten cross-modal alignment. Next, a heatmap-driven consensus protocol identifies exactly where cooperation is needed by computing per-pixel confidence heatmaps. Only the Top-K instance vectors located in these low-confidence, high-discrepancy regions are queried from peers, then fused via cross-attention for completion. Afterwards, we apply a refinement fusion that involves collecting the top-K most confident instances from each agent and enhancing their features using self-attention. The above instance-centric messaging reduces redundancy while guaranteeing that critical occluded objects are recovered. Evaluated on OPV2V and DAIR-V2X, EIMC attains 73.01\% AP@0.5 while reducing byte bandwidth usage by 87.98\% compared with the best published multi-modal collaborative detector. Code publicly released at https://github.com/sidiangongyuan/EIMC.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: A multi-stage distillation approach: (1) decouple representation learning from task learning—stage one selectively distills domain-agnostic features from a VFM teacher; (2) freeze learned representations and perform task-specific adaptation to reduce overfitting; plus a query-based soft distillation where student features query teacher representations to retrieve transferable spatial knowledge.

Abstract: Knowledge distillation (KD) has been widely applied in semantic segmentation to compress large models, but conventional approaches primarily preserve in-domain accuracy while neglecting out-of-domain generalization, which is essential under distribution shifts. This limitation becomes more severe with the emergence of vision foundation models (VFMs): although VFMs exhibit strong robustness on unseen data, distilling them with conventional KD often compromises this ability. We propose Generalizable Knowledge Distillation (GKD), a multi-stage framework that explicitly enhances generalization. GKD decouples representation learning from task learning. In the first stage, the student acquires domain-agnostic representations through selective feature distillation, and in the second stage, these representations are frozen for task adaptation, thereby mitigating overfitting to visible domains. To further support transfer, we introduce a query-based soft distillation mechanism, where student features act as queries to teacher representations to selectively retrieve transferable spatial knowledge from VFMs. Extensive experiments on five domain generalization benchmarks demonstrate that GKD consistently outperforms existing KD methods, achieving average gains of +1.9% in foundation-to-foundation (F2F) and +10.6% in foundation-to-local (F2L) distillation. Method: 1) Build a Confusion Bank capturing stable confusion relations and representative misclassified samples. 2) Semantic Confusion Miner (SEM) crafts semantic prompts that model inter-class differences and commonalities to capture global confusion signals. 3) Sample Confusion Miner (SAM) retrieves misclassified exemplars from the bank and uses a Diff-Manner Adapter to integrate global and local context for sample-level cues. 4) Multi-Granularity Difference Expert (MGDE) unifies semantic- and sample-level experts for joint confusion-aware reasoning. To address this, we propose CAPT, a Confusion-Aware Prompt Tuning framework that enables models to learn from their own misalignment. Specifically, we construct a Confusion Bank to explicitly model stable confusion relationships across categories and misclassified samples. Extensive experiments on 11 benchmark datasets demonstrate that our method significantly reduces confusion-induced errors while enhancing the discriminability and generalization of both base and novel classes, successfully resolving 50.72 percent of confusable sample pairs. TL;DR: Track4World is a feedforward, world-centric, per-pixel 3D tracker for monocular video that jointly predicts dense 2D optical flow and 3D scene flow via a VGGT-style ViT with a novel 3D correlation module, enabling efficient 4D reconstruction and outperforming prior methods on multiple benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Monocular 3D tracking is key for understanding video dynamics, but current approaches either track only sparse points from the first frame or rely on slow optimization for dense tracking. There is a need for an efficient, holistic, dense, per-pixel 3D tracking solution.

Method: Encode a global 3D scene representation with a VGGT-style Vision Transformer and introduce a 3D correlation scheme to simultaneously estimate pixel-wise 2D optical flow and 3D scene flow between arbitrary frame pairs. Combine the estimated scene flow with reconstructed 3D geometry to produce world-centric per-pixel trajectories in a fully feedforward manner.

Result: Across multiple benchmarks, the approach consistently surpasses existing methods in both 2D/3D flow estimation and 3D tracking accuracy, demonstrating robustness and scalability for real-world 4D reconstruction tasks.

Conclusion: A feedforward, world-centric framework that unifies dense 2D and 3D flow estimation with geometry reconstruction can deliver efficient, accurate per-pixel 3D tracking from monocular video, providing a practical path toward robust 4D reconstruction.

Abstract: Estimating the 3D trajectory of every pixel from a monocular video is crucial and promising for a comprehensive understanding of the 3D dynamics of videos. Recent monocular 3D tracking works demonstrate impressive performance, but are limited to either tracking sparse points on the first frame or a slow optimization-based framework for dense tracking. In this paper, we propose a feedforward model, called Track4World, enabling an efficient holistic 3D tracking of every pixel in the world-centric coordinate system. Built on the global 3D scene representation encoded by a VGGT-style ViT, Track4World applies a novel 3D correlation scheme to simultaneously estimate the pixel-wise 2D and 3D dense flow between arbitrary frame pairs. The estimated scene flow, along with the reconstructed 3D geometry, enables subsequent efficient 3D tracking of every pixel of this video. Extensive experiments on multiple benchmarks demonstrate that our approach consistently outperforms existing methods in 2D/3D flow estimation and 3D tracking, highlighting its robustness and scalability for real-world 4D reconstruction tasks.

### [36] [ATD: Improved Transformer with Adaptive Token Dictionary for Image Restoration](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02581)
*Leheng Zhang,Wei Long,Yawei Li,Xingyu Zhou,Xiaorui Zhao,Shuhang Gu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Proposes Adaptive Token Dictionary (ATD), a transformer that attains global dependency modeling with linear complexity via a learnable token dictionary and token-dictionary cross-attention; achieves SOTA on super-resolution and strong results on denoising and JPEG artifact removal.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Transformer self-attention is quadratically expensive, pushing image restoration models to local windows that limit receptive field and hurt performance. The goal is to keep global context while avoiding quadratic cost.

Method: Introduce a learnable token dictionary capturing typical image structures (external priors). Use Token Dictionary Cross-Attention (TDCA) to enrich input features by attending to this dictionary, yielding linear complexity with image size. Leverage TDCA attention maps to categorize features into groups (clusters of similar features) that serve as attention groups, and inject this category information into the feed-forward network for better fusion. Provide variants: ATD-light (compact) and ATD-U (multi-scale) for broader restoration tasks.

Result: ATD and ATD-light attain state-of-the-art performance on multiple super-resolution benchmarks. ATD-U effectively handles denoising and JPEG artifact removal. Extensive experiments show quantitative and qualitative superiority.

Conclusion: Learning a compact, global token dictionary and interacting with it via cross-attention enables efficient global modeling for image restoration. Category-aware grouping and integration into FFN further improve fusion, yielding strong, scalable performance across tasks with linear complexity.

Abstract: Recently, Transformers have gained significant popularity in image restoration tasks such as image super-resolution and denoising, owing to their superior performance. However, balancing performance and computational burden remains a long-standing problem for transformer-based architectures. Due to the quadratic complexity of self-attention, existing methods often restrict attention to local windows, resulting in limited receptive field and suboptimal performance. To address this issue, we propose Adaptive Token Dictionary (ATD), a novel transformer-based architecture for image restoration that enables global dependency modeling with linear complexity relative to image size. The ATD model incorporates a learnable token dictionary, which summarizes external image priors (i.e., typical image structures) during the training process. To utilize this information, we introduce a token dictionary cross-attention (TDCA) mechanism that enhances the input features via interaction with the learned dictionary. Furthermore, we exploit the category information embedded in the TDCA attention maps to group input features into multiple categories, each representing a cluster of similar features across the image and serving as an attention group. We also integrate the learned category information into the feed-forward network to further improve feature fusion. ATD and its lightweight version ATD-light, achieve state-of-the-art performance on multiple image super-resolution benchmarks. Moreover, we develop ATD-U, a multi-scale variant of ATD, to address other image restoration tasks, including image denoising and JPEG compression artifacts removal. Extensive experiments demonstrate the superiority of out proposed models, both quantitatively and qualitatively.

### [37] [Neural Electromagnetic Fields for High-Resolution Material Parameter Reconstruction](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02582)
*Zhe Chen,Peilin Zheng,Wenshuo Chen,Xiucheng Wang,Yutao Yue,Nan Cheng*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: NEMF is a framework that uses image-derived geometry and ambient RF signals, combined with differentiable physical reflection models, to invert for continuous, spatially varying material properties—turning an ill‑posed sensing problem into a well‑posed, physics-supervised learning task. Validated on synthetic data, it yields accurate material maps and functional digital twins suitable for high-fidelity simulation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Digital twins need not just appearance but material parameters (e.g., permittivity, conductivity) to simulate physical interactions. Existing vision methods (e.g., NeRF) lack these, and non-invasive recovery from remote signals is ill-posed because geometry, fields, and materials are entangled.

Method: Disentangle the problem by first anchoring with high-fidelity geometry from images. Use this to resolve the ambient RF field, then apply a decoder guided by ambient RF data and a differentiable reflection-physics layer to predict continuous, spatially varying material-property fields across the scene, reframing inversion as a physics-supervised learning problem.

Result: On high-fidelity synthetic datasets, the approach reconstructs dense material maps with high accuracy and enables simulations that closely match the underlying physics, producing functional digital twins rather than purely visual replicas.

Conclusion: Systematically constraining geometry and field enables non-invasive, dense estimation of material properties, moving from passive visual reconstructions to simulatable, functional twins. Abstract: Creating functional Digital Twins, simulatable 3D replicas of the real world, is a central challenge in computer vision. Current methods like NeRF produce visually rich but functionally incomplete twins. The key barrier is the lack of underlying material properties (e.g., permittivity, conductivity). Acquiring this information for every point in a scene via non-contact, non-invasive sensing is a primary goal, but it demands solving a notoriously ill-posed physical inversion problem. Standard remote signals, like images and radio frequencies (RF), deeply entangle the unknown geometry, ambient field, and target materials. We introduce NEMF, a novel framework for dense, non-invasive physical inversion designed to build functional digital twins. Our key insight is a systematic disentanglement strategy. NEMF leverages high-fidelity geometry from images as a powerful anchor, which first enables the resolution of the ambient field. By constraining both geometry and field using only non-invasive data, the original ill-posed problem transforms into a well-posed, physics-supervised learning task. This transformation unlocks our core inversion module: a decoder. Guided by ambient RF signals and a differentiable layer incorporating physical reflection models, it learns to explicitly output a continuous, spatially-varying field of the scene's underlying material parameters. We validate our framework on high-fidelity synthetic datasets. Experiments show our non-invasive inversion reconstructs these material maps with high accuracy, and the resulting functional twin enables high-fidelity physical simulation. This advance moves beyond passive visual replicas, enabling the creation of truly functional and simulatable models of the physical world.

### [39] [Synthetic-Child: An AIGC-Based Synthetic Data Pipeline for Privacy-Preserving Child Posture Estimation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.02598)
*Taowen Zeng*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Synthetic-Child introduces an AIGC pipeline that generates photorealistic, labeled child-posture data to train a compact, real-time pose/posture model that outperforms adult-data baselines—without using real child photos.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Collecting large, annotated datasets of children is expensive and ethically constrained by privacy, yet accurate child posture estimation is needed for AI study companions and similar applications.

Method: Four-stage pipeline: (1) SMPL-X child body in Blender creates diverse, IK-constrained desk-study poses with automatic COCO keypoints; (2) a PoseInjectorNode feeds 3D skeletons to dual ControlNet (pose+depth) with FLUX-1 Dev to synthesize 12k photorealistic images over 10 posture categories with low annotation drift; (3) ViTPose-based confidence filtering and targeted augmentation remove failures and improve robustness; (4) fine-tune RTMPose-M with geometric feature engineering plus a lightweight MLP for posture classification, then quantize to INT8 for edge use.

Result: On a real-child test set (~300 images), FP16 achieves 71.2 AP, a +12.5 AP gain over a COCO-pretrained adult-data baseline at the same capacity. After INT8 quantization, performance is 70.4 AP at 22 FPS on a 0.8-TOPS RK3568 NPU. In a single-subject controlled comparison, the system recognizes more categories and responds ~1.8× faster than a commercial posture corrector.

Conclusion: Well-engineered synthetic data pipelines can substantially reduce reliance on real child imagery while delivering deployment-ready accuracy, with potential applicability to other privacy-sensitive domains.

Abstract: Accurate child posture estimation is critical for AI-powered study companion devices, yet collecting large-scale annotated datasets of children is both expensive and ethically prohibitive due to privacy concerns. We present Synthetic-Child, an AIGC-based synthetic data pipeline that produces photorealistic child posture training images with ground-truth-projected keypoint annotations, requiring zero real child photographs. The pipeline comprises four stages: (1) a programmable 3D child body model (SMPL-X) in Blender generates diverse desk-study poses with IK-constrained anatomical plausibility and automatic COCO-format ground-truth export; (2) a custom PoseInjectorNode feeds 3D-derived skeletons into a dual ControlNet (pose + depth) conditioned on FLUX-1 Dev, synthesizing 12,000 photorealistic images across 10 posture categories with low annotation drift; (3) ViTPose-based confidence filtering and targeted augmentation remove generation failures and improve robustness; (4) RTMPose-M (13.6M params) is fine-tuned on the synthetic data and paired with geometric feature engineering and a lightweight MLP for posture classification, then quantized to INT8 for real-time edge deployment. On a real-child test set (n~300), the FP16 model achieves 71.2 AP -- a +12.5 AP improvement over the COCO-pretrained adult-data baseline at identical model capacity. After INT8 quantization the model retains 70.4 AP while running at 22 FPS on a 0.8-TOPS Rockchip RK3568 NPU. In a single-subject controlled comparison with a commercial posture corrector, our system achieves substantially higher recognition rates across most tested categories and responds ~1.8x faster on average. These results demonstrate that carefully designed AIGC pipelines can substantially reduce dependence on real child imagery while achieving deployment-ready accuracy, with potential applications to other privacy-sensitive domains.

*A. Enes Doruk,Hasan F. Ates*

  <summary>Details</summary>

InstVLM (Instance-driven VLM Attention) uses gated cross-attention with LoRA-adapted CLIP embeddings to inject semantic and geographic priors into 3D voxels. WeathFusion dynamically gates and reweights sensor contributions using vehicle metadata and weather-conditioned prompts. A Depth-Aware Geometric Alignment (DAGA) loss enforces consistency between dense camera-derived geometry and sparse, accurate LiDAR returns. The modules are plug-and-play for voxel-based baselines.

Abstract: This paper introduces VLMFusionOcc3D, a robust multimodal framework for dense 3D semantic occupancy prediction in autonomous driving. To address these challenges, we leverage the rich linguistic priors of Vision-Language Models (VLMs) to anchor ambiguous voxel features to stable semantic concepts. Our framework initiates with a dual-branch feature extraction pipeline that projects multi-view images and LiDAR point clouds into a unified voxel space. We propose Instance-driven VLM Attention (InstVLM), which utilizes gated cross-attention and LoRA-adapted CLIP embeddings to inject high-level semantic and geographic priors directly into the 3D voxels. Furthermore, we introduce Weather-Aware Adaptive Fusion (WeathFusion), a dynamic gating mechanism that utilizes vehicle metadata and weather-conditioned prompts to re-weight sensor contributions based on real-time environmental reliability. To ensure structural consistency, a Depth-Aware Geometric Alignment (DAGA) loss is employed to align dense camera-derived geometry with sparse, spatially accurate LiDAR returns. Extensive experiments on the nuScenes and SemanticKITTI datasets demonstrate that our plug-and-play modules consistently enhance the performance of state-of-the-art voxel-based baselines. Notably, our approach achieves significant improvements in challenging weather scenarios, offering a scalable and robust solution for complex urban navigation.

*Zhikang Xu,Qianqian Xu,Zitai Wang,Cong Hua,Sicong Li,Zhiyong Yang,Qingming Huang*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: InterNeg uses inter-modal distance in two coordinated ways: (1) Textual perspective: applies an inter-modal criterion to select effective negative texts relative to ID labels. (2) Visual perspective: dynamically identifies high-confidence OOD images and inverts them into the textual space to create additional negative text embeddings, all guided by inter-modal distances for OOD scoring.

However, current methods often incorporate intra-modal distance during OOD detection, such as comparing negative texts with ID labels or comparing test images with image proxies. This design paradigm creates an inherent inconsistency against the inter-modal distance that CLIP-like VLMs are optimized for, potentially leading to suboptimal performance. To address this limitation, we propose InterNeg, a simple yet effective framework that systematically utilizes consistent inter-modal distance enhancement from textual and visual perspectives. From the textual perspective, we devise an inter-modal criterion for selecting negative texts. From the visual perspective, we dynamically identify high-confidence OOD images and invert them into the textual space, generating extra negative text embeddings guided by inter-modal distance. Extensive experiments across multiple benchmarks demonstrate the superiority of our approach. Notably, our InterNeg achieves state-of-the-art performance compared to existing works, with a 3.47\% reduction in FPR95 on the large-scale ImageNet benchmark and a 5.50\% improvement in AUROC on the challenging Near-OOD benchmark.

In this paper, we delve into the negative effect of spurious and redundant features on this dilemma in incremental unified frameworks, and reveal that under similar conditions, the multimodal framework developed by naive aggregation of unimodal architectures is more prone to forgetting. To address this issue, we introduce a novel denoising framework called IB-IUMAD, which exploits the complementary benefits of the Mamba decoder and information bottleneck fusion module: the former dedicated to disentangle inter-object feature coupling, preventing spurious feature interference between objects; the latter serves to filter out redundant features from the fused features, thus explicitly preserving discriminative information.   <summary>Details</summary>

The goal is to strengthen modality grounding so that the model is sensitive to the correct modality and invariant to irrelevant ones, thereby reducing unintended cross-modal interactions and text-only biases.

Method: Extend Direct Preference Optimization with modality-aware regularization: (1) enforce invariance when the non-relevant modality is corrupted; (2) enforce sensitivity when the relevant modality is perturbed; and (3) add a language-prior debiasing penalty that discourages text-only, hallucination‑prone responses. Train under similar budgets as prior PO methods.

Result: Across multiple audiovisual hallucination benchmarks, MoD-DPO consistently boosts perception accuracy and hallucination resistance, outperforming existing preference-optimization baselines under comparable training budgets.

Abstract: Omni-modal large language models (omni LLMs) have recently achieved strong performance across audiovisual understanding tasks, yet they remain highly susceptible to cross-modal hallucinations arising from spurious correlations and dominant language priors. In this work, we propose Modality-Decoupled Direct Preference Optimization (MoD-DPO), a simple and effective framework for improving modality grounding in omni LLMs. MoD-DPO introduces modality-aware regularization terms that explicitly enforce invariance to corruptions in irrelevant modalities and sensitivity to perturbations in relevant modalities, thereby reducing unintended cross-modal interactions. To further mitigate over-reliance on textual priors, we incorporate a language-prior debiasing penalty that discourages hallucination-prone text-only responses. Extensive experiments across multiple audiovisual hallucination benchmarks demonstrate that MoD-DPO consistently improves perception accuracy and hallucination resistance, outperforming previous preference optimization baselines under similar training budgets. Our findings underscore the importance of modality-faithful alignment and demonstrate a scalable path toward more reliable and resilient multimodal foundation models.

We introduce DREAM, a unified framework that jointly optimizes discriminative and generative objectives, while learning strong visual representations. DREAM is built on two key techniques: During training, Masking Warmup, a progressive masking schedule, begins with minimal masking to establish the contrastive alignment necessary for representation learning, then gradually transitions to full masking for stable generative training. Trained solely on CC12M, DREAM achieves 72.7% ImageNet linear-probing accuracy (+1.1% over CLIP) and an FID of 4.25 (+6.2% over FLUID), with consistent gains in few-shot classification, semantic segmentation, and depth estimation. *Yong Eun Choi,Hyoung Suk Park,Kiwan Jeon,Hyun-Cheol Park,Sung Ho Kang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: ReCo-Diff introduces residual-conditioned, self-guided sampling for cold/generalized diffusion to reconstruct sparse-view CT, using the measurement residual at each step to correct predictions under a deterministic schedule, yielding more accurate, stable, and robust reconstructions than existing baselines.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current cold/generalized diffusion samplers for sparse-view CT rely on ad hoc controls or fixed schedules that can accumulate errors and destabilize sampling. A principled, measurement-aware correction mechanism is needed to improve reconstruction fidelity and stability without heuristic tuning.

Method: At every sampling step, first compute a null (unconditioned) baseline reconstruction. Then compute the observation residual between the predicted image and the measured sparse-view input, and condition the next prediction on this residual. This residual-driven guidance provides continuous, measurement-aware correction while preserving a deterministic sampling schedule, eliminating heuristic interventions.

Result: Across experiments, ReCo-Diff consistently outperforms cold diffusion sampling baselines, achieving higher reconstruction accuracy, improved sampling stability, and stronger robustness, particularly under severe view sparsity.

Conclusion: Residual-conditioned self-guided sampling effectively leverages measurement residuals to steer diffusion-based CT reconstruction, mitigating error accumulation and instability while maintaining a deterministic schedule, and delivers superior performance to prior cold diffusion methods.

Abstract: Cold and generalized diffusion models have recently shown strong potential for sparse-view CT reconstruction by explicitly modeling deterministic degradation processes. However, existing sampling strategies often rely on ad hoc sampling controls or fixed schedules, which remain sensitive to error accumulation and sampling instability. We propose ReCo-Diff, a residual-conditioned diffusion framework that leverages observation residuals through residual-conditioned self-guided sampling. At each sampling step, ReCo-Diff first produces a null (unconditioned) baseline reconstruction and then conditions subsequent predictions on the observation residual between the predicted image and the measured sparse-view input. This residual-driven guidance provides continuous, measurement-aware correction while preserving a deterministic sampling schedule, without requiring heuristic interventions. Experimental results demonstrate that ReCo-Diff consistently outperforms existing cold diffusion sampling baselines, achieving higher reconstruction accuracy, improved stability, and enhanced robustness under severe sparsity.

To bridge this gap, we propose CoR-Painter, a novel framework that pioneers a "How-to-What" paradigm by introducing Constrained Reasoning to guide the autoregressive generation. Specifically, it first deduces "How to draw" by deriving a set of visual constraints from the input prompt, which explicitly govern spatial relationships, key attributes, and compositional rules. These constraints steer the subsequent generation of a detailed description "What to draw", providing a structurally sound and coherent basis for accurate visual synthesis. Additionally, we introduce a Dual-Objective GRPO strategy that specifically optimizes the textual constrained reasoning and visual projection processes to ensure the coherence and quality of the entire generation pipeline. Linear attention offers $\mathcal{O}(N)$ scaling, but often exhibits training instability and attention dilution, yielding diffuse maps. We introduce PVT-GDLA, a decoder-centric Transformer that restores sharp, long-range dependencies at linear time. Its core, Gated Differential Linear Attention (GDLA), computes two kernelized attention paths on complementary query/key subspaces and subtracts them with a learnable, channel-wise scale to cancel common-mode noise and amplify relevant context.
